### [1] [SymTFT Approach for Mixed States with Non-Invertible Symmetries](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05350)
*Sakura Schafer-Nameki,Apoorv Tiwari,Alison Warman,Carolyn Zhang*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究mixing 状态下强弱对称为体的相变问题，构建一个把Density matrix纯化的框架，并在双Hilbert空间用SymTFT进行分类。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 在量子场论和量子statistical mechanics中，研究对称性，尤其是mixing 状态下的对称性变化是一个重要问题。这类问题需要构建普适的分析框架来理解和分类相行为。

Method: 该研究通过将混合态的density matrix 纯化，并将其嵌入到双Hilbert空间，利用对称性拓扑场论的方法进行分类。

Result: 该框架适用于强对称性和弱对称性（包括非可逆对称性），可以分类1+1维情况下的强对称性保护的拓扑相以及强和弱对称性的混合相。

Conclusion: 成功构建了一个适用于强弱对称性的相分类框架，特别是在涉及非可逆对称性的场合具有普适性，为量子相变的研究提供了强有力的工具。

Abstract: We develop a general framework for studying phases of mixed states with
strong and weak symmetries, including non-invertible or categorical symmetries.
The central idea is to consider a purification of the mixed state density
matrix, which lives in a doubled Hilbert space. We propose a systematic
classification of phases in this doubled Hilbert space, relying crucially on
the Symmetry Topological Field Theory (SymTFT) approach. This framework applies
not only to group symmetries but also, importantly, to non-invertible
symmetries. We illustrate the approach in 1+1d to classify phases with strong
(non-)invertible symmetries, which include strong-to-weak spontaneous symmetry
breaking (SWSSB) phases and mixed strong/weak symmetry-protected topological
phases (SPTs). We also develop an approach for studying symmetries that involve
a combination of strong and weak symmetries. A noteworthy example of this has
weak non-invertible Kramers-Wannier duality symmetry and strong $\mathbb{Z}_2$
symmetry. The continuum description is complemented by a lattice model analysis
informed by the SymTFT framework.

</details>


### [2] [Looking elsewhere: improving variational Monte Carlo gradients by importance sampling](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05352)
*Antoine Misery,Luca Gravina,Alessandro Santini,Filippo Vicentini*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究提出了一种自适应重要性采样方法来改进神经网络量子态的变分蒙特卡罗训练。方法通过自适应调整采样策略来降低梯度估计的方差，不增加额外的超参数，且计算开销低。实验结果显示该方法显著提高了训练效率。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 量子计算中的神经网络量子态（NQS）模型在表示量子多体波函数方面表现优异，但其训练中使用变分蒙特卡洛方法时遇到挑战。特别是处理像量子化学中的高峰波函数这样的复杂场景时，会产生高方差的梯度估计，影响优化效果。因此，研究者提出了自适应重要性采样方法来解决这些问题。

Method: 研究采用自适应的重要性采样方法，并将其应用到变分蒙特卡罗方法中。具体来说，通过动态调整采样策略来集中采样高概率区域，从而降低梯度估计的方差。研究者设计的这种方法无需增加额外的超参数，并且计算开销较低。

Result: 实验结果表明，该自适应重要性采样方法显著提升了变分蒙特卡罗方法的效率。特别是在处理复杂量子化学问题时，计算成本降低了大约100倍。

Conclusion: 该研究提供了一种有效的自适应重要性采样方法，显著提升了神经网络量子态变分蒙特卡罗训练的效率和稳定性。这种方法具有广泛的应用前景，尤其是在处理具有高峰波函数的量子体系问题时。

Abstract: Neural-network quantum states (NQS) offer a powerful and expressive ansatz
for representing quantum many-body wave functions. However, their training via
Variational Monte Carlo (VMC) methods remains challenging. It is well known
that some scenarios - such as sharply peaked wave functions emerging in quantum
chemistry - lead to high-variance gradient estimators hindering the
effectiveness of variational optimizations. In this work we investigate a
systematic strategy to tackle those sampling issues by means of adaptively
tuned importance sampling. Our approach is explicitly designed to (i) target
the gradient estimator instead of the loss function, (ii) not introduce
additional hyperparameters and (iii) be computationally inexpensive. We
benchmarked our approach across the ground-state search of a wide variety of
hamiltonians, including frustrated spin systems and ab-initio quantum
chemistry. We also show systematic improvements on the infidelity minimization
in the context of neural projected quantum dynamics. Overall, our approach can
reduce the computational cost of vanilla VMC considerably, up to a factor of
100x when targeting highly peaked quantum chemistry wavefunctions.

</details>


### [3] [Unified Framework for Quantum Code Embedding](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05361)
*Andrew C. Yuan*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper explores embedding CSS codes, providing mathematical tools for ensuring logical qubit preservation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: It discusses embedding quantum codes to maintain logical qubits, useful in quantum error correction.

Method: Uses homological algebra, specifically topological codes and their properties.

Result: Direction for constructing isomorphic codes using topological frameworks.

Conclusion: A general method is presented, integrating prior works through algebraic methods.

Abstract: Given a Calderbank-Shor-Steane (CSS) code, it is sometimes necessary to
modify the stabilizer code by adding an arbitrary number of physical qubits and
parity checks. Motivations may include embedding a high-dimensional quantum
low-density parity check (LDPC) code into finite-dimensional Euclidean space,
or reducing the weights of an arbitrary CSS code. During this embedding, it is
essential that the modified CSS code possesses an isomorphic set of logical
qubits as the original CSS code. However, despite numerous explicit
constructions, the conditions of when such a property holds true is not known
in general. Therefore, using the language of homological algebra, we provide a
unified framework that guarantees a natural isomorphism between the output and
input codes. In particular, we explicitly show how previous works fit into our
framework.

</details>


### [4] [Simultaneous Determination of Local Magnetic Fields and Sensor Orientation with Nitrogen-Vacancy Centers in Nanodiamond](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05366)
*Yizhou Wang,Haochen Shen,Zhongyuan Liu,Yue Yu,Shengwang Du,Chong Zu,Chuanwei Zhang*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究使用纳米金刚石中的氮- Celebren-维中心作为量子传感器，解决了粒子朝向不一的问题，通过施加不同偏场来同时确定晶体轴和局部磁场。该方法在 bulk diamond 和单个纳米金刚石上进行了验证，为生物医学成像和纳米传感器应用铺平了道路。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 量子传感器在生物医学成像和纳米tier sensing中具有重要应用价值，但纳米金刚体的晶体取向不一导致大规模校准困难，故研究提出解决方法。

Method: 至少4个不同的偏场施加来 simultaneously确定晶体轴和局部磁场。在 bulk diamond和单个纳米金刚体上进行实验验证。

Result: verify了该方法在 bulk 和单个纳米金刚体上的有效性，展示了_calibrating 过程和应用潜力。

Conclusion: 研究为解锁纳米金刚体在生物医学成像和复杂环境中的应用奠定了基础。

Abstract: Nitrogen-vacancy (NV) centers in nanodiamonds have emerged as a promising
quantum sensing platform for biomedical imaging applications, yet random
orientations of individual particles present significant challenges in
large-scale sensor calibration. In this study, we demonstrate a novel approach
to simultaneously determine each particle's crystallographic axes and the
surrounding local vector magnetic field. Specifically, a minimum of four
distinct bias fields is required to unambiguously extract both the orientation
and the local field. We validate our method experimentally using NV centers in
two scenarios: (1) in a bulk diamond with known crystal orientation as a proof
of concept, and (2) on various single nanodiamonds to mimic real-world
applications. Our work represents a crucial step towards unlocking the full
potential of nanodiamonds for advanced applications such as in-situ biomedical
imaging and nanoscale sensing in complex environments.

</details>


### [5] [Superior Frequency Stability and Long-Lived State-Swapping in Cubic-SiC Mechanical Mode Pairs](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05646)
*Huanying Sun,Yanlin Chen,Qichun Liu,Haihua Wu,Yuqing Wang,Tiefu Li,Yulong Liu*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 该研究利用多模式腔 optomechanical 系统，通过集成 3C-SiC 憜片和矩形容器超导腔，观察到近退化机械模式对的产生。并导出了非均匀应力下的固有频率表达式，其分析精度在薄片应力分析中表现卓越。实验中通过收集 57 个机械模式的测量数据进行集体拟合，揭示了双轴非均匀应力偏差，大小达到 MPa 级别。这些非退化解的机械模式具有极高的品质因数，在 10 mK 热浴中达到 $10^8$。此外，利用阿伦方差发现，这些模式的频率稳定性优于其他 optomechanical 设备。通过使近退化模对发生态交换，获得了超过 78% 的转移效率，归因于其极长的寿命。该研究为高质机械量子声子器件的设计提供了理论基础。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 该论文涉及 optomechanical 系统在量子声子器件设计中的应用，表现出了一系列优异的性能指标，值得深入分析其方法和潜在应用。

Method: 该研究通过集成 3C-SiC 憜片和矩形容器超导腔，构建了腔电声子系统。实验中测量并分析了 57 个机械模式，使用集体拟合技术，计算出非均匀应力下的固有频率，并通过阿伦方差评估频率稳定性。状态交换实验中，状态转移效率超过 78%，归因于长时间寿命。

Result: 研究展示了高质因素、极高的频率稳定性和高效的态交换性能，为量子声子器件提供了性能基准。

Conclusion: 该研究为设计具有高质因数和长寿命的量子声子器件提供了真实可行的技术途径。

Abstract: The multimode cavity optomechanical system offers versatile applications
including state transduction, coherent interconnection, and many-body
simulations. In this study, we developed a cavity electromechanical system that
integrates a 3C-SiC membrane and a rectangular superconducting cavity to
observe the generation of nearly degenerate pairs of mechanical modes.
Subsequently, we derive the expression for intrinsic frequency under nonuniform
stress and find that this method supports a remarkably resolution for stress
analysis in thin films. Experimentally, we perform collective fitting on the
measured set of 57 mechanical modes, revealing deviations in biaxial
non-uniform stress on the order of MPa. These degeneracy-broken mechanical
modes exhibit exceptional quality factors as high as $10^8$ in a thermal bath
of 10 mK. Furthermore, Allan deviation indicates that these modes exhibit
extremely stable frequencies compared with different types of optomechanical
devices. We then performed state-swapping between near-degenerate mode pairs,
demonstrating the transfer efficiency exceeding 78\%, attributed to their
exceptionally long lifetimes. This study paves the way for the design of
compact quantum phononic devices featuring high-quality-factor mechanical
multimode.

</details>


### [6] [Universal Long-Time Behavior of the Quantum Fisher Information in Dynamical Quantum Phase Transitions](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05579)
*J. Mumford,R. J. Lewis-Swan*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究DQPT的量子玻色爱因斯坦凝聚和利普金-梅什科夫-吉克模型，使用量子 Fisher信息长期平均来诊断相变，发现其在相变点发生突变，并且展示出系统的通用行为。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究量子系统中的相变现象，尤其是没有经典极限的情况，有助于深入理解量子相变的内在机制。

Method: 使用量子 Fisher信息作为诊断工具，结合均场和半经典方法进行分析。

Result: 在相变点，量子 Fisher信息的长期平均会发生突变，呈现出系统的通用行为。

Conclusion: 系统在DQPT处显示出与经典系统相似的长期量子行为，有助于建立普遍适用的理论框架。

Abstract: We investigate dynamical quantum phase transitions (DQPTs) in quantum systems
that possess well-defined classical limits, focusing on the spinor
Bose-Einstein condensate and the Lipkin-Meshkov-Glick model. We diagnose the
DQPTs with the long-time average of the quantum Fisher information (QFI)
showing that it abruptly changes at the transition point. Using mean-field and
semiclassical approximations, we demonstrate that the long-time average of the
QFI reveals universal behavior that persists across different systems.

</details>


### [7] [Geometric Invariants of Quantum Metrology](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.06128)
*Christopher Wilson,John Drew Wilson,Luke Coffman,Shah Saad Alam,Murray J. Holland*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: We discovered a new conservation law for the Quantum Fisher Information Matrix (QFIM) tied to Lie algebras. The QFIM's spectrum remains unchanged under unitary operations generated by these algebras, meaning the metrological sensitivity is fixed. This reminds us of Liouville's theorem and has implications for classifying quantum states using geometric methods, similar to classical optimality criteria.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper introduces an innovative approach by linking quantum Fisher information with Lie algebras and unitary dynamics, aiming to uncover new fundamental properties in quantum metrology.

Method: The method used involves analyzing the behavior of QFIM under unitary transformations generated by Lie algebras to identify conserved quantities and invariants.

Result: The key result is a conservation law for QFIM's spectrum, implying fixed metrological capabilities based on symmetry groups, similar to how squeezing affects sensitivity in interferometry.

Conclusion: This finding offers a new way to classify quantum states by their Lie algebra symmetry, using geometric invariants for metrological analysis, extending classical optimality concepts.

Abstract: We establish a previously unexplored conservation law for the Quantum Fisher
Information Matrix (QFIM) expressed as follows; when the QFIM is constructed
from a set of observables closed under commutation, i.e., a Lie algebra, the
spectrum of the QFIM is invariant under unitary dynamics generated by these
same operators. Each Lie algebra therefore endows any quantum state with a
fixed "budget" of metrological sensitivity -- an intrinsic resource that we
show, like optical squeezing in interferometry, cannot be amplified by
symmetry-preserving operations. The Uhlmann curvature tensor (UCT) naturally
inherits the same symmetry group, and so quantum incompatibility is similarly
fixed. As a result, a metrological analog to Liouville's theorem appears;
statistical distances, volumes, and curvatures are invariant under the
evolution generated by the Lie algebra. We discuss this as it relates to the
quantum analogs of classical optimality criteria. This enables one to
efficiently classify useful classes of quantum states at the level of Lie
algebras through geometric invariants.

</details>


### [8] [Solving Large-Scale Vehicle Routing Problems with Hybrid Quantum-Classical Decomposition](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05373)
*Andrew Maciejunes,John Stenger,Dan Gunlycke,Nikos Chrisochoides*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 该研究提出了一个两层分解方法，结合量子近似优化算法（QAOA）来解决大型车辆路径问题（VRP）。通过问题级和电路级分解，将13节点VRP分解成TSP，并在近端量子设备上执行，显著减少了电路深度、所需的量子位数和双量子位门数。实验结果表明，该方法适用于复杂度高的VRP问题，展示了量子计算早期的实用价值。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 随着量子计算的快速发展，解决NP难问题成了研究热点。而VRP作为组合优化问题之一，特别是大规模VRP，一直难以在量子计算上处理。该论文提出了一种结合分解策略和QAOA的方法，可能为解决更大规模的VRP提供了新思路。

Method: 两层分解策略，先进行问题级分解将VRP分解为TSP，再进行电路级分解，进一步细分成更小部分，适合量子设备执行。通过这种方法，在减小电路深度、减少量子位数和双量子位门数方面表现出色。

Result: 该方法在标准边编码和 novel 幅度编码下表现出优异性能，达到了95%、96%和99.5%的性能提升，证明了该方法在解决复杂VRP方面有效性。

Conclusion: 该研究展示了通过分解策略和QAOA解决复杂VRP的可能性，为量子计算在组合优化中的应用提供了新方法。未来研究可以扩展该方法至更大规模问题。

Abstract: We present a two-level decomposition strategy for solving the Vehicle Routing
Problem (VRP) using the Quantum Approximate Optimization Algorithm. A
Problem-Level Decomposition partitions a 13-node (156-qubit) VRP into smaller
Traveling Salesman Problem (TSP) instances. Each TSP is then further cut via
Circuit-Level Decomposition, enabling execution on near-term quantum devices.
Our approach achieves up to 95\% reductions in the circuit depth, 96\%
reduction in the number of qubits and a 99.5\% reduction in the number of
2-qubit gates. We demonstrate this hybrid algorithm on the standard edge
encoding of the VRP as well as a novel amplitude encoding. These results
demonstrate the feasibility of solving VRPs previously too complex for quantum
simulators and provide early evidence of potential quantum utility.

</details>


### [9] [Engineering giant transmon molecules as mediators of conditional two-photon gates](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05377)
*Tomás Levy-Yeyati,Tomás Ramos,Alejandro González-Tudela*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 论文利用非局部耦合的超导微球构建了小型态，设计了一个被动光子受控门，分析了其条件和性能。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究者希望利用超导微球构建小型态，和超导电路制造量子计算中的受控门。

Method: 研究通过非局部耦合和分子束缚效应结合，利用超导微球在波导中的相互作用设计了受控门，结合致密分析了性能。

Result: 成功实现了被动光子受控门，并通过分析非局部耦合、分子束缚和非线性效应，得到了最大π相移的条件及门的信噪比。

Conclusion: 研究开启了用超导原子作为量子计算中光子量子设备的关键组件。

Abstract: Artificial atoms non-locally coupled to waveguides -- the so-called giant
atoms -- offer new opportunities for the control of light and matter. In this
work, we show how to use an array of non-locally coupled transmon "molecules"
to engineer a passive photonic controlled gate for waveguide photons. In
particular, we show that a conditional elastic phase shift between
counter-propagating photons arises from the interplay between
direction-dependent couplings, engineered through an interplay of non local
interactions and molecular binding strength; and the nonlinearity of the
transmon array. We analyze the conditions under which a maximal $\pi$-phase
shift -- and hence a CZ gate -- is obtained, and characterize the gate fidelity
as a function of key experimental parameters, including finite transmon
nonlinearities, emitter spectral inhomogeneities, and limited cooperativity.
Our work opens the use of giant atoms as key elements of microwave photonic
quantum computing devices.

</details>


### [10] [Probing Defects with Quantum Simulator Snapshots](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05379)
*Abhijat Sarma,Nayan Myerson-Jain,Roger G. Melko,Cenke Xu*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The study introduces a protocol using snapshots from a quantum system to detect and analyze defects by analyzing spin configurations, specifically showing how to extract defect entropy and access fixed point properties.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper proposes a method to observe and analyze defects in quantum systems through existing experimental data without altering the system, which is particularly useful for studying criticality and phase transitions.

Method: The protocol utilizes snapshots of local spin configurations from bulk systems to probe defects. It extracts defect entropy by analyzing phase structure and accesses fixed points through Renyi entropies of clusters.

Result: Experiments with Rydberg atoms in 1D demonstrate the protocol's effectiveness in extracting defectrelated information and accessing phase transitions, providing new insights into critical phenomena.

Conclusion: The presented method offers a practical, alternative approach to study defects using standard measurement techniques, opening new avenues for research in quantum critical systems and phase transitions.

Abstract: Snapshots, i.e. projective measurements of local degrees of freedom, are the
most standard data taken in experiments on quantum simulators. Snapshots are
usually used to probe local physics. In this work we propose a simple protocol
to experimentally probe physics of defects with these snapshots. Our protocol
relies only on snapshots from the bulk system, without introducing the defect
explicitly; as such, the physics of different kinds of defects can be probed
using the same dataset. In particular, we demonstrate that with snapshots of
local spin configurations of, for example, the $1d$ Rydberg atom realization of
the quantum Ising criticality, we can (1) extract the ``defect entropy", and
(2) access the continuous line of fixed points of effective defect conformal
field theory, which was recently discussed in the context of the
``weak-measurement altered criticality".

</details>


### [11] [Asymptotically Good Quantum Codes with Addressable and Transversal Non-Clifford Gates](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05392)
*Zhiyang He,Vinod Vaikuntanathan,Adam Wills,Rachel Yun Zhang*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 该论文提出了一种新的量子纠错码构造方法，能够在较低码长和较好参数下支持非门道可执行的逻辑CCZ门。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 量子计算中的量子错误纠正是其中之一最重要的基础问题。构造具有良好参数和实用纠错能力的量子编码以及支持高效执行非门道可执行的逻辑门是研究领域的核心难题。该论文在现有研究基础上，提出了新的编码构造方法，有效地解决了这一难题，为量子计算的应用提供了更有力的技术支撑。

Method: 论文基于代数几何码，结合量子纠错码和可执行逻辑门的研究，提出了一种新的编码构造方法。该方法采用可交换正交代数几何码并结合可逆正交编译器，能够通过物理电路中深度一的CCZ门来实现任意三个逻辑量子位的CCZ门操作。

Result: 该编码在较低码长和更高的码速率下，能够支持非门道可执行的逻辑CCZ门操作。相对于之前的构造，该编码在速率和码距上有显著改进。

Conclusion: 该研究方法展示了代数几何码在量子纠错码设计中的独特优势，并为量子计算中的复杂操作提供了更高效的解决方案。该成果对量子计算的发展具有重要意义，具有广阔的应用前景。

Abstract: Constructing quantum codes with good parameters and useful transversal gates
is a central problem in quantum error correction. In this paper, we continue
our work in arXiv:2502.01864 and construct the first family of asymptotically
good quantum codes (over qubits) supporting transversally addressable
non-Clifford gates. More precisely, given any three logical qubits across one,
two, or three codeblocks, the logical $\mathsf{CCZ}$ gate can be executed on
those three logical qubits via a depth-one physical circuit of $\mathsf{CCZ}$
gates. This construction is based on the transitive, iso-orthogonal algebraic
geometry codes constructed by Stichtenoth (IEEE Trans. Inf. Theory, 2006). This
improves upon our construction from arXiv:2502.01864, which also supports
transversally addressable $\mathsf{CCZ}$ gates and has inverse-polylogarithmic
rate and relative distance.

</details>

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究兴趣在于物理位的强噪声干扰下如何实现可靠的量子操作，寻找在单一主导错误类型编码下的高效量子门实施方法。

Method: 借助编码理论，分析了经典同相位错误校正码和量子无相位编码的限制，探讨了通用逻辑门集所需的电路构造，最后尝试通过魔力态合成改进性能。

Abstract: With the advent of physical qubits exhibiting strong noise bias, it becomes
increasingly relevant to identify which quantum gates can be efficiently
implemented on error-correcting codes designed to address a single dominant
error type. Here, we consider $[n,k,d]$-classical stabilizer codes addressing
bit-flip errors where $n$, $k$ and $d$ are the numbers of physical and logical
qubits, and the code distance respectively. We prove that operations essential
for achieving a universal logical gate set necessarily require complex unitary
circuits to be implemented. Specifically, these implementation circuits either
consists of $h$ layers of $r$-transversal operations on $c$ codeblocks such
that $c^{h-1}r^h \geq d$ or of $h$ gates, each operating on at most $r$
physical qubits on the same codeblock, such that $hr\geq d$. Similar
constraints apply not only to classical codes designed to correct phase-flip
errors, but also to quantum stabilizer codes tailored to biased noise. This
motivates a closer examination of alternative logical gate constructions using
eg.~magic state distillation and cultivation within the framework of
biased-noise stabilizer codes.

### [15] [An order-theoretic circuit syntax and characterisation of the concept lattice](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05428)

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The research introduces a new mathematical framework for analyzing and restructuring circuits, which is relevant to quantum computing and causality. The authors aim to formalize these structures for better understanding and manipulation of circuit components.

Method: The authors use an order-theoretic approach, defining circuits as partial orders with input-output structures, prove a factorization theorem regarding morphisms, and link circuit connectivity to concept lattices for quantum causality applications.

Result: The factors established in the paper include formalizing circuit rewrites, defining quotient maps as gate compositions, an optimal circuit for a given connectivity, and a dual characterization of circuits.

Conclusion: The paper provides a comprehensive mathematical framework for circuit restructurings and studies the role of circuit connectivity in quantum causation, offering significant insights for synthesizing and analyzing causal unitary transformations and their duals.

Abstract: We take an order-theoretic approach to circuit (string diagram) syntax,
treating a circuit as a partial order with additional input-output structure.
We define morphisms between circuits and prove a factorisation theorem showing
that these can, in the finite case, be regarded as formalising a notion of
syntactical circuit rewrites, with quotient maps in particular corresponding to
gate composition. We then consider the connectivity of a circuit, expressed as
a binary relation between its inputs and outputs, and characterise the concept
lattice from formal concept analysis as the unique smallest circuit that admits
morphisms from all other circuits with the same connectivity. This has
significance for quantum causality, particularly to the study of causal
decompositions of unitary transformations. We close by constructing the circuit
characterised by the dual statement.

### [18] [Wave/particle duality in monitored Jaynes--Cummings resonances](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05837)
*Th. K. Mavrogordatos*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper examines wave-particle duality in the strong coupling limit of the Jaynes-Cummings model, focusing on vacuum Rabi resonance and non-classical properties of light fields. They calculate intensity correlation functions and find non-classical behavior, photon blockade effects, and nonclassical phase shifts in conditioned fields. The addition of photon injection restores classical behavior. Temporal symmetry is reduced but overall coherence is maintained in steady states.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Constructing a theoretical framework to explain quantum phenomena in open quantum systems allows us to understand fundamental aspects of light-matter interactions, particularly wave-particle duality. The Jaynes-Cummings model, a foundational model in quantum optics, provides a suitable framework to study these phenomena. The strong coupling limit is especially relevant for understanding real experimental systems and potential applications in quantum technologies. This paper contributes to this goal by exploring these aspects in detail using existing theoretical tools and numerical methods.

Method: The authors employ a combination of analytical and numerical methods. They use mapping to ordinary resonance fluorescence to derive the intensity correlation functions for the system under study. They analyze the system in the strong coupling limit using perturbative and exact numerical techniques, such as diagonalization, to study the dynamics near vacuum Rabi resonance.

Result: The main results highlight the non-classical nature of light fields associated with vacuum Rabi oscillations, the role of photon blockade in altering the frequency of fluctuations, and the occurrence of non-classical phase shifts in the conditioned fields when considering additional injection of photons. They find that introducing photon injection into the system restores detailed balance and produces an almost classical high-frequency quantum beat in the conditioned fields. The population statistics reveal that near the two-photon resonance, the system exhibits a bimodal distribution of photon numbers in the cavity, which reduces the variation in the intensity correlation functions but does not eliminate their temporal asymmetry.

Conclusion: The paper contributes to understanding the characteristics of wave-particle duality in open quantum systems by providing a detailed analysis of the Jaynes-Cummings model under strong coupling conditions. Their findings demonstrate the complex interplay between quantum effects and classical-like behavior, especially under different system conditions. The results offer insights into the potential for controlling and manipulating quantum interference effects in such systems, which is essential for the development of quantum optics-based technologies, including quantum information processing and quantum metrology. The balance between non-classical effects and classical behavior under different perturbations opens up new avenues for research into quantum-to-classical transitions in open quantum systems.

Abstract: We operationally uncover aspects of wave/particle duality for the open driven
Jaynes-Cummings (JC) model in its strong-coupling limit. We lay special
emphasis on the vacuum Rabi resonance, and determine the corresponding
normalized intensity-field correlation function via mapping to ordinary
resonance fluorescence. We demonstrate that temporal wave-particle fluctuations
of light emanating from an established vacuum Rabi resonance are explicitly
non-classical, while the limit of vanishing spontaneous emission restores
detailed balance. When photon blockade sets in, individual realizations show a
rapidly increasing frequency of fluctuations towards the two-photon resonance,
arising as a direct consequence of a resolved JC spectrum. About the two-photon
resonance peak, spontaneous emissions are more likely to revive a
high-frequency quantum beat in the conditioned electromagnetic field amplitude
than photons escaping out of the cavity mode. The beat originates from a
coherent superposition of the first excited JC couplet states, and sets the
background against which nonclassical phase shifts are observed in the
conditioned quadrature amplitudes. We also find that the onset of steady-state
bimodality reduces the variation of the normalized intensity-field correlation,
at the expense of its temporal symmetry.

Abstract: Non-Hermitian systems possess exotic localization phenomena beyond their
Hermitian counterparts, exhibiting massive accumulation of eigenstates at the
system boundaries with different scaling behaviors. In this study, we
investigate two weakly coupled non-Hermitian Hatano-Nelson chains under

other. Notably, the localization characteristics of eigenstates can exchange
between the two chains depending on their eigenenergies. This phenomenon is
found to emerge from the critical behaviors induced by the weak interchain

### [22] [Special-Unitary Parameterization for Trainable Variational Quantum Circuits](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05535)
*Kuan-Cheng Chen,Huan-Hsin Tseng,Samuel Yen-Chi Chen,Chen-Yu Liu,Kin K. Leung*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR:  paper proposes a new quantum variational circuit (SUN-VQC) that uses Lie subalgebra to improve performance and overcome barren plateaus. They use exact gradients, avoid ancilla qubits, and show better results in quantum auto-encoding and classification.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Variational quantum algorithms are promising for near-term quantum computing, but they suffer from issues like the barren plateau problem. This paper addresses that by designing a more efficient circuit architecture using Lie subalgebra.

Method: The paper introduces SUN-VQC, which restricts each layer to a symmetrical Lie subgroup SU(2^k) within a larger SU(2^n). This reduces the dynamical Lie-algebra dimension, leading to lower gradient variance and avoiding barren plateaus. They employ a generalized parameter-shift rule for exact gradients without using ancillary qubits or finite-difference bias.

Result: Numerical experiments on quantum auto-encoding and classification demonstrate that SUN-VQC circuits outperform Pauli-rotation and hardware-efficient circuits, with larger gradient signals, faster convergence, and higher final fidelities.

Conclusion: The Lie-subalgebra engineering provides a scalable and principled approach to developing more robust quantum variational algorithms that can effectively use near-term quantum processors.

Abstract: We propose SUN-VQC, a variational-circuit architecture whose elementary
layers are single exponentials of a symmetry-restricted Lie subgroup,
$\mathrm{SU}(2^{k}) \subset \mathrm{SU}(2^{n})$ with $k \ll n$. Confining the
evolution to this compact subspace reduces the dynamical Lie-algebra dimension
from $\mathcal{O}(4^{n})$ to $\mathcal{O}(4^{k})$, ensuring only polynomial
suppression of gradient variance and circumventing barren plateaus that plague
hardware-efficient ans\"atze. Exact, hardware-compatible gradients are obtained
using a generalized parameter-shift rule, avoiding ancillary qubits and
finite-difference bias. Numerical experiments on quantum auto-encoding and
classification show that SUN-VQCs sustain order-of-magnitude larger gradient
signals, converge 2--3$\times$ faster, and reach higher final fidelities than
depth-matched Pauli-rotation or hardware-efficient circuits. These results
demonstrate that Lie-subalgebra engineering provides a principled, scalable
route to barren-plateau-resilient VQAs compatible with near-term quantum
processors.

</details>

Abstract: Photon counting is a fundamental component in quantum optics and quantum
information. However, implementing ideal photon-number-resolving (PNR)
detectors remains experimentally challenging. Multiplexed PNR detection offers
a scalable and practical alternative by distributing photons across multiple
modes and detecting their presence using simple ON-OFF detectors, thereby
enabling approximate photon-number resolution. In this work, we establish a
theoretical model for such detectors and prove that the estimation error in
terms of photon number moments decreases inverse proportionally to the number

subtraction case, 7dB of squeezing, and an array of 20 detectors of efficiency
95%, our calculation predicts fidelity ~ 0.88 with a success probability ~
3.8%, representing orders-of-magnitude improvement over previous works. Similar
enhancement also extends to cat-state generation with the generalized photon
number subtraction. With experimentally feasible parameters, our results
suggest that megahertz-rate cat-state generation is achievable using an on-chip
array of tens of ON-OFF detectors.

light-matter interactions approaches the resonance frequencies of light and

Abstract: We present a scalable framework for accurately modeling many-body

### [26] [Tensor network algorithm to solve polaron impurity problems](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05580)
*Ruofan Chen,Lei Gu,Chu Guo*

Main category: quant-ph

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 随着量子计算和Condensed Matter Physics的发展，功能性更强的量子模拟方法显得尤为重要。现有的CT量子蒙特卡罗方法通常受限于只能在imaginary-time轴上处理，而无法灵活处理其他类型的路径积分contour。同时，面对复杂的电子电子相互作用和电子声子相互作用，现有数值方法要么计算复杂度过高，要么不可行。

Method: 引入张量网络和路径积分方法，通过Feynman-Vernon影响泛函消除了声子 baths的离散化误差，支持在imaginary、Keldysh以及L-shaped Kadanoff contour上工作。

Result: 通过与解析解、精确对角化和现有CT量子蒙特卡罗方法的对比，证明了该方法的有效性和准确性；成功完成了首次实时间计算，为未来方法开发提供了基准。

Conclusion: 该新方法克服了现有CT量子蒙特卡罗方法的局限性，扩展了计算能力，特别是在处理复杂相互作用和测量多时间相关函数方面表现优异，具有广泛应用前景。

Abstract: The polaron problem is a very old problem in condensed matter physics that
dates back to the thirties, but still remain largely unsolved today, especially
when electron-electron interaction is taken into consideration. The presence of
both electron-electron and electron-phonon interactions in the problem
invalidates most existing numerical methods, either computationally too
expensive or simply intractable. The continuous time quantum Monte Carlo
(CTQMC) methods could tackle this problem, but are only effective in the
imaginary-time axis. In this work we present a method based on tensor network
and the path integral formalism to solve polaron impurity problems. As both the
electron and phonon baths can be integrated out via the Feynman-Vernon
influence functional in the path integral formalism, our method is free of bath
discretization error. It can also flexibly work on the imaginary, Keldysh, and
the L-shaped Kadanoff contour. In addition, our method can naturally resolve
several long-existing challenges: (i) non-diagonal hybridization function; (ii)
measuring multi-time correlations beyond the single particle Green's functions.
We demonstrate the effectiveness and accuracy of our method with extensive
numerical examples against analytic solutions, exact diagonalization and CTQMC.
We also perform full-fledged real-time calculations that have never been done
before to our knowledge, which could be a benchmarking baseline for future
method developments.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究者希望改善量子测量中的反馈控制技术，以减少测量的随机性带来的影响。

Method: 通过分析连续时间测量的量子轨迹，研究一种反馈协议来消除噪声，证明了在理想条件下这种协议的存在，并用实证例子如纠缠态制备和稳定测试来验证其有效性，还应用于魔力态分发协议，提升了成功率。

Result: 得出噪声消除反馈协议在量子态准备和保护中有效，特别是在魔力态分发中的成功率提高显著。

Conclusion: 讨论了噪声消除反馈在量子纠缠态和魔力态分发中的应用效果，强调其在提升成功概率和抗错能力中的重要性。itives提升显著，适合应用于需要稳定量子态的量子计算和通信任务。

Abstract: Time-continuous quantum measurement allows for the tracking of a quantum
system in real time via sequences of short, and individually weak, measurement
intervals. Such measurements are necessarily invasive, imparting backaction to
the system, and allowing the observer to update their state estimate based on
stochastic measurement outcomes. Feedback control then involves real-time
interventions by an observer, conditioned on the time-continuous measurement
signal that they receive. We here consider diffusive quantum trajectories, and
focus on the "noise-canceling" subset of feedback protocols that aim to
minimize the degree of stochasticity in the dynamics. We derive such a class of
feedback operations, showing that under the idealized assumptions of pure
states, unit measurement efficiency, and zero time-delay in implementing
feedback operations, perfectly noise-canceling feedback always exists. We
consider the resulting noise-canceled dynamics generated by an effective
non-Hermitian Hamiltonian; while non-Hermitian Hamiltonians from continuous
monitoring generally describe rare dynamics (accessible by costly
post-selection), the use of noise-canceling feedback here leads to
non-Hermitian dynamics that occur deterministically. We demonstrate this via
examples of entangled state preparation and stabilization. We then illustrate
the potential for the application of noise-cancellation to boost success rates
in magic state distillation protocols. We show that adding feedback based on
noise-cancellation into a time-continuous 5-to-1 distillation protocol leads to
higher probabilities of successful distillation across a range of input errors,
and extends the threshold on input errors for which the protocol is effective.
Our results highlight the efficacy of noise-canceling feedback-aided protocols
for quantum state preparation and stabilization tasks.

### [28] [Learnable quantum spectral filters for hybrid graph neural networks](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05640)
*Ammar Daskin*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: paper introduces a quantum circuit for graph neural networks with convolutional and pooling layers, using QFT and Laplacian eigenspace to achieve efficient compression and improved performance on geometric graph tasks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: the paper addresses the challenge of applying quantum computing to graph learning, particularly for tasks involving geometric structures, by developing an efficient quantum circuit that mimics classical graph convolutional layers but with reduced computational complexity.

Method: the paper proposes a parameterized quantum circuit based on the quantum Fourier transform (QFT) and the Laplacian operator's eigenspace approximation. The method leverages the structure of the graph through its adjacency matrix to determine controlled gates, resulting in a circuit that reduces the number of qubits required from N to log(N) while maintaining the functionality of convolutional and pooling layers.

Result: experiments on benchmark datasets using the TUDataset library show that the quantum-enhanced graph neural network achieves competitive or superior performance compared to classical baseline methods, especially when the geometric structure of the graph is significant for the task.

Conclusion: this work represents a promising step toward utilizing quantum resources for graph-based learning tasks, demonstrating that quantum circuits can be effectively integrated into graph neural networks to improve their performance on certain types of graph-structured data. the method achieves this by leveraging the graph's inherent structure through its Laplacian connections, reducing the necessary qubits and maintaining the functionality needed for effective learning.

Abstract: In this paper, we describe a parameterized quantum circuit that can be
considered as convolutional and pooling layers for graph neural networks. The
circuit incorporates the parameterized quantum Fourier circuit where the qubit
connections for the controlled gates derived from the Laplacian operator.
Specifically, we show that the eigenspace of the Laplacian operator of a graph
can be approximated by using QFT based circuit whose connections are determined
from the adjacency matrix. For an $N\times N$ Laplacian, this approach yields
an approximate polynomial-depth circuit requiring only $n=log(N)$ qubits. These
types of circuits can eliminate the expensive classical computations for
approximating the learnable functions of the Laplacian through Chebyshev
polynomial or Taylor expansions.
  Using this circuit as a convolutional layer provides an $n-$ dimensional
probability vector that can be considered as the filtered and compressed graph
signal. Therefore, the circuit along with the measurement can be considered a
very efficient convolution plus pooling layer that transforms an
$N$-dimensional signal input into $n-$dimensional signal with an exponential
compression. We then apply a classical neural network prediction head to the
output of the circuit to construct a complete graph neural network. Since the
circuit incorporates geometric structure through its graph connection-based
approach, we present graph classification results for the benchmark datasets
listed in TUDataset library. Using only [1-100] learnable parameters for the
quantum circuit and minimal classical layers (1000-5000 parameters) in a
generic setting, the obtained results are comparable to and in some cases
better than many of the baseline results, particularly for the cases when
geometric structure plays a significant role.

### [29] [Quantum Latin squares with all possible cardinalities](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05642)
*Ying Zhang,Xin Wang,Lijun Ji*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper introduces quantum Latin squares (QLS) and their substructures, proving the existence of QLS(4m) with specific cardinalities by constructing them using sub-QLS(4)s.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper aims to explore the combinatorial properties of quantum Latin squares, extending classical Latin squares into the quantum domain. By proving the existence of QLS(4m) with certain cardinalities, it contributes to quantum information theory and potentially quantum computing applications.

Method: The authors utilize sub-QLS(4)s, which are smaller quantum Latin squares, to construct larger QLS(4m). They employ combinatorial and algebraic methods to demonstrate that for each m ≥ 2, and for cardinalities c in the range [4m, 16m²] excluding 4m+1, such QLS(4m) can be built by assembling these sub-QLS(4)s appropriately.

Result: The paper successfully constructs quantum Latin squares of order 4m with cardinalities c in the specified range, providing a deeper understanding of their structure and combinatorial properties.

Conclusion: The study significantly advances the understanding of quantum Latin squares by leveraging their substructures, demonstrating their potential in quantum technologies like quantum error correction and quantum algorithms.

Abstract: A quantum Latin square of order $n$ (denoted as QLS$(n)$) is an $n\times n$
array whose entries are unit column vectors from the $n$-dimensional Hilbert
space $\mathcal{H}_n$, such that each row and column forms an orthonormal
basis. Two unit vectors $|u\rangle, |v\rangle\in \mathcal{H}_n$ are regarded as
identical if there exists a real number $\theta$ such that
$|u\rangle=e^{i\theta}|v\rangle$; otherwise, they are considered distinct. The
cardinality $c$ of a QLS$(n)$ is the number of distinct vectors in the array.
In this paper, we use sub-QLS$(4)$s to prove that for any integer $m\geq 2$ and
any integer $c\in [4m,16m^2]\setminus \{4m+1\}$, there is a QLS$(4m)$ with
cardinality $c$.

</details>


### [30] [Additivity of quantum relative entropies as a single-copy criterion](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05696)
*Salman Beigi,Roberto Rubboli,Marco Tomamichel*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: This paper discusses the necessity of regularization in quantum information tasks, showing that for certain problems, single-copy optimization suffices, leading to computable characterizations using additive quantities.enstein exponents are derived for hypothesis testing and resource theories, with conditions established for additivity.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Quantum information theory often relies on regularized entropic measures, which can be difficult to compute. This paper investigates scenarios where regularization is unnecessary, simplifying computations by using single-copy optimization instead.

Method: The authors introduce a property of a single-copy optimizer that determines whether regularization is needed for a given problem. They apply this to hypothesis testing with varying hypotheses and quantum resource theories related to entanglement and magic state distillation. Stein, Chernoff, and Hoeffding exponents are computed, and conditions for their additivity are established. Additionally, partial results on the strong converse exponent are provided.

Result: The paper shows that regularization is not needed for a class of problems if and only if a single-copy optimizer has a specific property. This leads to additive characterizations based on the Umegaki relative entropy and related quantities. They derive exponents for hypothesis testing and resource theories, establish additivity conditions, and present partial results on the strong converse exponent.

Conclusion: By linking the necessity of regularization to properties of single-copy optimization, the paper advances our understanding of efficient computation in quantum information tasks, impacting areas like entanglement and magic state distillation.

Abstract: The fundamental goal of information theory is to characterize complex
operational tasks using efficiently computable information quantities,
Shannon's capacity formula being the prime example of this. However, many tasks
in quantum information can only be characterized by regularized entropic
measures that are often not known to be computable and for which efficient
approximations are scarce. It is thus of fundamental importance to understand
when regularization is not needed, opening the door to an efficiently
computable characterization based on additive quantities. Here, we demonstrate
that for a large class of problems, the question of whether regularization is
needed or not can be determined at the single-copy level. Specifically, we
demonstrate that regularization of the Umegaki relative entropy, along with
related quantities such as the Petz and sandwiched relative entropies, is not
needed if and only if a single-copy optimizer satisfies a certain property.
These problems include hypothesis testing with arbitrarily varying hypotheses
as well as quantum resource theories used to derive fundamental bounds for
entanglement and magic state distillation. We derive the Stein, Chernoff, and
Hoeffding exponents for these problems and establish necessary and sufficient
conditions for their additivity, while also presenting partial results for the
strong converse exponent.

</details>

Abstract: Thermal engines have been one of the principal topics of thermodynamics ever
since its beginning. Today, in the era of the second quantum revolution,
although the thermal processes in constant temperatures are relatively well
understood in the language of resource theories, a framework to describe
thermal engines is still in its infancy. In this work we formalize the resource
theory of engines, initially put forward in [Quantum 8, 1222], and define such
quantities as engine efficiency. Then, we turn to a detailed study of thermal

operations and local thermal operation with classical communication. In order

tree-states -- free states, which can be obtained from Gibbs state in simple

full description of the engine based on semilocal thermal operations describing
e.g. free states, faithful monotones and catalytic advantages.

### [32] [Mixed states for reference frames transformations](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05758)
*Gaetano Fiore,Fedele Lizzi*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper discusses transformations between reference frames in classical and quantum contexts. In classical scenarios, transformations are sharply defined and form groups, but in quantum cases, they can form semigroups and involve mixed states, leading to non-pure transformations. This has implications for how system states relate to different reference frames and their applications to time-temperature connections.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper introduces a novel exploration of reference frame transformations, both classical and quantum, suggesting that these transformations can be either pure or mixed. This is motivated by the notion that quantum systems often involve mixed states, which are not always accounted for in traditional transformations, leading to potential applications in connecting different physical parameters like time and temperature.

Method: The authors employ abstract mathematical reasoning, considering the structure of possible transformations as groups or semigroups in classical and quantum cases. They use concepts from linear algebra, such as states being pure or mixed, to model the transformations.

Result: The key result is that transformations among quantum reference frames can be mixed, unlike classical transformations which form groups. This results in systems appearing pure under one frame but mixed under another, with implications for thermodynamic quantities like time and inverse temperature.

Conclusion: The paper concludes that non-pure transformations are natural in quantum reference frames and provides an application example in connecting time and inverse temperature for thermal states. This offers a new perspective on reference frame transformations in quantum mechanics.

Abstract: We discuss the concept of transformations among reference frames (classical
or quantum). Usually transformations among classical reference frames have
sharply defined parameters; geometrically they can be considered as pure states
in the parameters' space, and they form a group. It is however possible that
the distributions in the parameters' space are mixed state; such states form a
semigroup. Similarly, transformations among quantum reference frames can be
either pure or mixed. This gives rise to interesting consequences, in
particular, the state of a system S can be pure with respect to a reference
frame and mixed with respect to another. We argue that these nonpure
transformations are natural, and give an application to the connections of time
and (inverse) temperature for thermal states.

</details>


### [33] [Observation of hierarchy of Hilbert space ergodicities in the quantum dynamics of a single spin](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05706)
*Wenquan Liu,Zouwei Pan,Yue Fu,Wei Cheng,Wen Wei Ho,Xing Rong,Jiangfeng Du*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究通过不同时间依赖的驱动手段，验证了量子系统的海abolic行为。结果显示，在周期驱动下没有海波性，在准周期驱动下有部分海波性，而在斐波那契驱动下实现了完整的海波性。这种方法可能促进量子系统达到平衡的机制研究。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 探索量子系统如何达到平衡状态，以及不同时间驱动方式对量子系统动力学的影响。

Method: 实验中使用单核磁共振仪观察单量子自旋，通过全状态扫描实时追踪驱动后的轨迹，对比不同驱动模式下的海波特性。

Result: 通过不同驱动模式显示，为了实现海波性，驱动模式的复杂度至关重要。

Conclusion: 提出了一种新的实验方法用于测试量子系统的海波特性，为理解量子系统平衡提供了直接证据。

Abstract: Ergodicity, the property that all allowed configurations are explored over
time, plays a pivotal role in explaining the equilibrium behavior of classical
dynamical systems. Yet, such a property is typically precluded in quantum
systems owing to the presence of energy eigenstates, which are stationary
states in dynamics. However, recent theoretical works have argued that ergodic
explorations of the Hilbert space, occurring at varying levels as measured by
statistical pseudorandomness of the time-evolved quantum states, may be
exhibited for quantum systems driven by Hamiltonians with aperiodic time
dependencies, which do not face such obstacles. Here, we experimentally
investigate the hierarchy of Hilbert-space ergodicities (HSE) achievable in the
dynamics of a single quantum spin realized by a solid-state defect in diamond,
upon subjecting it to various time-dependent modulations. Through continuous
monitoring of spin trajectories with full state tomography, different degrees
of HSE were observed, ranging from no HSE in a time-periodic (Floquet) drive,
to partial HSE in a smoothly kicked time-quasiperiodic drive, to complete HSE
in a drive composed of a sequence of kicks generated by the Fibonacci word. We
formulate a theoretical understanding of the increasing levels of HSE observed
by attributing them to increasing levels of complexities associated with the
drive sequences, whose notions we elucidate. Our work constitutes the first
unambiguous experimental evidence of Hilbert space ergodicity and promotes
deeper investigations into the mechanisms and fine-grained levels with which
closed quantum systems reach equilibrium.

</details>

reservoir-engineered optical parametric oscillator (OPO). The OPO provides a
basis of squeezed states and parametric amplification in lasing emission, whose
vacuum reservoir is coupled to a squeezed vacuum generated by a second OPO.
With a precisely controlled squeezing angle and strong squeezing injection, the
parametric interaction in the first OPO is exponentially enhanced. It
successfully circumvents the decoherence in the system, and eliminates the
undesired noise of spontaneous photon emission in the OPO. As a result, the
amplified parametric process simultaneously reserves the coherence and quantum
properties in the first OPO, and yields a -6.1 dB squeezed laser in optical
domain with a narrow linewidth and high brightness. Our work sheds light on
potential applications of squeezed lasing in quantum metrology and quantum
optics.

</details>

Abstract: Quantum state discrimination is a fundamental concept in quantum information
theory, which refers to a class of techniques to identify a specific quantum
state through a positive operator-valued measure. In this work, we investigate
how structural information about either the quantum states or the measurement
operators can influence our ability to determine or bound the optimal
discrimination probability. First, we observe that for single-qubit states,
pairwise fidelities are sufficient to completely characterize the optimal
discrimination. In contrast, for multi-qubit states, this correspondence breaks
down. Motivated by this, we analytically derive the optimal discrimination
probability for three equiprobable single-qubit states with equal pairwise
fidelities in terms of fidelity. Secondly, we consider partial information
about the optimal measurement, specifically the measurement operators that
vanish in the optimal solution. We show that such information can be leveraged
to tighten existing upper bounds on the optimal discrimination probability.
Lastly, we show that in some cases, subsets and supersets of nonvanishing
operators can be identified without semidefinite programming.

### [38] [Reconstruction of Noise from Dynamical Mode Decomposition in Quantum Systems](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05797)
*Adva Baratz,Loris Maria Cangemi,Assaf Hamo,Sivan Refaely-Abramson,Amikam Levy*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper presents a new method using DMD and constrained extrapolation to analyze quantum noise, showing promising results in extracting spectral features and coherence decay.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding noise in quantum systems is crucial for improving their performance and reliability.

Method: The authors use Dynamical Mode Decomposition (DMD) combined with constrained extrapolation to analyze quantum dynamics under stochastic noise.

Result: The method can effectively extract spectral features and dephasing times like T2* from experimental data, showing potential for diagnostic and predictive analysis.

Abstract: Noise fundamentally limits the performance of quantum systems by degrading
coherence and reducing control fidelity. Characterizing this noise is essential
for improving measurement accuracy, understanding environmental interactions,
and designing effective control strategies. However, extracting its spectral
characteristics and associated dephasing times from limited experimental data
remains a key challenge.
  Here, we introduce a data-driven framework based on Dynamical Mode
Decomposition (DMD) to analyze the dynamics of quantum systems under stochastic
noise. We reinterpret DMD modes as statistical weights over an ensemble of
quantum trajectories and use this mapping to construct a noise power spectral
density (PSD) via a nonlinear transformation. This enables identification of
dominant frequency contributions in both white and $1/f$ noise environments and
directly yields the pure dephasing time $T_2^*$ from DMD eigenvalues. To
overcome instability in standard DMD reconstruction, we develop a constrained
extrapolation scheme using the extracted $T_2^*$ as a physical bound and the
learned PSD as mode weights. We demonstrate our method on simulated Ramsey-type
dynamics and validate its ability to recover spectral features and coherence
decay. This approach offers a robust, data-driven tool for diagnostic and
predictive noise analysis in quantum systems.

### [41] [Matrix-product entanglement characterizing the optimality of state-preparation quantum circuits](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05989)
*Shuo Qi,Wen-Jun Li,Gang Su,Shi-Ju Ran*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 多体纠缠提供了一种强大的框架，用于理解量子多体系统中的复杂集体现象，这些现象常常用常规的双分纠缠度量无法描述。这里我们提出了一类基于矩阵乘积态（MPS）表示的多体纠缠度量，从而可以表征向前 engineered 量子电路在状态准备中的最优性。这些度量被定义为与目标态到带指定虚拟电荷维度χ的MPS流形的最小距离，因此被命名为χ-指定的矩阵乘积纠缠度（χ-MPE）。我们展示了χ-MPE相对于负对数保真度F的超线性、线性和亚线性缩放行为，这些分别对应于准备χ-维虚拟MPS所必需的电路深度D过大、最优和不足。具体情况下，当χ-MPE随着F线性增长时，表明两个流形χ和D是等价的。我们对χ=2的等式进行了精确证明，即Hχ=2≡HD=1。我们的结果表明了张量网络作为有效的参数化量度多体纠缠度量的一种强大的和通用工具。采用了χ-MPE的矩阵乘积形式可以在其他张量网络方案中轻易地扩展，其缩放行为可以评估相应张量网络态的前向engineered量子电路的最优性。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 探索新物理现象和理解复杂量子系统的行为在量子物理和量子信息科学中是至关重要的。提出新的纠缠度量方法对于评估量子系统的复杂性和资源消耗具有重要意义。

Method: 该论文提出了一种基于矩阵乘积态的多体纠缠度量，称为χ-指定的矩阵乘积纠缠度（χ-MPE）。通过计算目标态与特定电荷维度χ的MPS流形的最小距离，该度量表征了量子电路的最优性。研究了χ-MPE在不同电路深度D下的缩放行为，包括超线性、线性和亚线性行为，并通过证明当χ=2时，χ-MPE等同于D=1的情况，展示了其通用性。

Result: 主要结果包括：1. 多体纠缠度量χ-MPE能通过评估状态准备所需电路深度，表征量子电路的最优性。2. χ-MPE的缩放行为为超线性、线性和亚线性，对应电路深度过大、最优和不足。3. 精确证明了当χ=2时，χ-MPE等同于D=1的情况，展示了方法的有效性和普适性。

Conclusion: 该研究展示了张量网络方法在量子多体系统研究中的广泛适用性。提出了具有实用意义的新纠缠度量χ-MPE，并为使用张量网络架构设计高效的量子电路提供了理论基础。将这种方法扩展到其他类型的张量网络架构，能够深入评估不同架构下的量子资源和计算能力。

Abstract: Multipartite entanglement offers a powerful framework for understanding the
complex collective phenomena in quantum many-body systems that are often beyond
the description of conventional bipartite entanglement measures. Here, we
propose a class of multipartite entanglement measures that incorporate the
matrix product state (MPS) representation, enabling the characterization of the
optimality of quantum circuits for state preparation. These measures are
defined as the minimal distances from a target state to the manifolds of MPSs
with specified virtual bond dimensions $\chi$, and thus are dubbed as
$\chi$-specified matrix product entanglement ($\chi$-MPE). We demonstrate
superlinear, linear, and sublinear scaling behaviors of $\chi$-MPE with respect
to the negative logarithmic fidelity $F$ in state preparation, which correspond
to excessive, optimal, and insufficient circuit depth $D$ for preparing
$\chi$-virtual-dimensional MPSs, respectively. Specifically, a linearly-growing
$\chi$-MPE with $F$ suggests $\mathcal{H}_{\chi} \simeq \mathcal{H}_{D}$, where
$\mathcal{H}_{\chi}$ denotes the manifold of the $\chi$-virtual-dimensional
MPSs and $\mathcal{H}_{D}$ denotes that of the states accessible by the $D$
layer circuits. We provide an exact proof that $\mathcal{H}_{\chi=2} \equiv
\mathcal{H}_{D=1}$. Our results establish tensor networks as a powerful and
general tool for developing parametrized measures of multipartite entanglement.
The matrix product form adopted in $\chi$-MPE can be readily extended to other
tensor network ans\"atze, whose scaling behaviors are expected to assess the
optimality of quantum circuit in preparing the corresponding tensor network
states.

### [43] [Instance-Optimal Quantum State Certification with Entangled Measurements](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.06010)
*Ryan O'Donnell,Chirag Wadhwa*

TL;DR: 研究论文讨论量子态确认问题，证明了当测试者可以进行全纠缠测量时，几乎最优的复制复杂性边界，基于状态与最大混合态的去相干率。使用Ingster-Suslina方法的量子扩展作为下界证明工具。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 当前量子信息处理领域，特别是在量子状态确认方面，如何在每个实例（即特定σ和ρ）下优化所需资源是一个关键问题。这项研究通过证明一个几乎最优的下界，显著地推进了这一领域的发展，尤其是在允许全纠缠测量的限制条件下。

Method: 该研究应用了量子化的Ingster-Suslina方法作为下界证明工具，并扩展了这一方法以适应复杂度优化所需的场景。同时，研究还展示了该方法如何简化并重新证明了混合态认证的下界。

Result: 研究得出，当允许全纠缠测量时，量子态确认（即σ与ρ是否相同或ε相距）所需的近似最优复制复杂度为Ω(d/ε²)，其中去相干率考虑状态与最大混合态之间的差异。

Abstract: We consider the task of quantum state certification: given a description of a
hypothesis state $\sigma$ and multiple copies of an unknown state $\rho$, a
tester aims to determine whether the two states are equal or $\epsilon$-far in
trace distance. It is known that $\Theta(d/\epsilon^2)$ copies of $\rho$ are
necessary and sufficient for this task, assuming the tester can make entangled
measurements over all copies [CHW07,OW15,BOW19]. However, these bounds are for
a worst-case $\sigma$, and it is not known what the optimal copy complexity is
for this problem on an instance-by-instance basis. While such instance-optimal
bounds have previously been shown for quantum state certification when the
tester is limited to measurements unentangled across copies [CLO22,CLHL22],
they remained open when testers are unrestricted in the kind of measurements
they can perform.
  We address this open question by proving nearly instance-optimal bounds for
quantum state certification when the tester can perform fully entangled
measurements. Analogously to the unentangled setting, we show that the optimal
copy complexity for certifying $\sigma$ is given by the worst-case complexity
times the fidelity between $\sigma$ and the maximally mixed state. We prove our
lower bounds using a novel quantum analogue of the Ingster-Suslina method,
which is likely to be of independent interest. This method also allows us to
recover the $\Omega(d/\epsilon^2)$ lower bound for mixedness testing [OW15],
i.e., certification of the maximally mixed state, with a surprisingly simple
proof.

</details>

Abstract: Interferometry can be viewed generally as the measurement of a relative phase

### [45] [Quantum tunneling in the time periodic double well potential](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.06045)

Method: 构建双势阱模型，偶次势能，使用数值算法求解Schrödinger方程，通过改变调制参数观察隧道速率的变化。

Result: 获得调制下波函数隧道的调节规律，发现频率调制能显著影响隧道速率。

Conclusion: 时间调制可调控量子系统的隧道效应，结果为相关领域的技术开发提供了理论基础。

Abstract: We present the mathematical model and numerical calculation results for the
tunneling of the wave function in a time-periodic double-well potential. The
bi-quadratic potential of a double-well form is used. Based on a mathematical
model of the time evolution of the wave function, a numerical algorithm has
been developed and a program has been created for solving the Schr\"odinger
equation, which describes the time evolution of the particle's wave function.
As a result of numerical modeling, modulation regimes have been obtained at
which tunneling took place. In a stationary double well potential, no tunneling
was observed. On the contrary, in the time periodic potential, tunneling was
observed, the rate of which depended on the modulation frequency. Adjusting the
modulation parameters, it is possible to control the particle wave function
tunneling rate.

Abstract: In classical information theory, uncommon information refers to the amount of
information that is not shared between two messages, and it admits an

computed exactly in the classical case, no direct method is currently known for

propose a new approach for estimating these bounds by utilizing the quantum

method. Our results suggest a pathway toward efficient approximation of quantum
uncommon information using variational techniques grounded in quantum neural
architectures.

Abstract: Quantum error correction (QEC) requires the execution of deep quantum

measurement circuits. However, they typically introduce high-weight correlated
errors that can degrade the circuit-level distance, leading to slower scalings
of the logical error probabilities. In this work, we show how to realize fast
and efficient surface code stabilizer readout using only two $CZ_2$ gates --
instead of four $CZ$ -- while preserving fault tolerance, and provide a
blueprint for implementation in Rydberg atom arrays. We derive the time-optimal
pulses implementing the gates and perform extensive QEC numerical simulations
with leakage errors. Compared to the standard protocol using four $CZ$ gates,
our scheme is faster, uses fewer gates and crucially maintains fault tolerance

### [49] [What's my phase again? Computing the vacuum-to-vacuum amplitude of quadratic bosonic evolution](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.06154)
*Nicolás Quesada*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 摘要讨论了二次bosonicHamiltonians及其相关的unitary变换在量子光学中的重要性，提出了一种利用真空到真空振幅恢复相位的方法，该方法在多模式情况下具有多项式复杂度。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 作者意识到在量子光学中，描述光子操作的Hamiltonians的二次型在Heisenberg图景下可以简化为线性或仿射变换，但忽略了相位这一重要信息。

Method: 提出了一种通过真空到真空振幅的计算来恢复相位，避免了Fock空间计算，简化了分析过程。

Result: 能够有效地恢复相位信息，适用于包括正定、被动和主动等不同类型的Hamiltonians。

Conclusion: 该方法提供了有效的工具，用于光子操作的完整分析和分解。

Abstract: Quadratic bosonic Hamiltonians and their associated unitary transformations
form a fundamental class of operations in quantum optics, modeling key
processes such as squeezing, displacement, and beam-splitting. Their
Heisenberg-picture dynamics simplifies to linear (or possibly affine)
transformations on quadrature operators, enabling efficient analysis and
decomposition into optical gate sets using matrix operations. However, this
formalism discards a phase, which, while often neglected, is essential for a
complete unitary characterization. We present efficient methods to recover this
phase directly from the vacuum-to-vacuum amplitude of the unitary, using
calculations that scale polynomially with the number of modes and avoid Fock
space manipulations. We reduce to integration the general problem, including
the case of time-dependent Hamiltonians, and provide analytical results for key
cases including when the Hamiltonian is positive definite, passive, active, or
single-mode.

### [50] [How the Kerr-Cat Qubit Dies-And How to Rescue It](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.06160)
*Othmane Benhayoune-Khadraoui,Cristóbal Lledó,Alexandre Blais*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 实验发现使用Kerr-cat qubit增强驱动时会减弱其优势，可能的原因是环路中的多能态。”,


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 这项研究在超导电路实现中的Kerr-cat qubit显示了一些有趣的特性，特别是在增强驱动信号可能导致错误地增强噪声的情况下，如何保持_coherence_重要性。

Method: 通过精确的Floquet-Markov分析，考虑强驱动，保留环路的非线性，发现多能态可能导致问题。

Result: 结果显示出当驱动超过临界值时，环路中的多能态激发出很强的多能态共振，导致Kerr-cat qubit的coherence急剧下降，无法提高tunneling时间。

Conclusion: 为适当选择环路参数，可以通过强驱动来增强Kerr-cat qubit的coherence，并在存在环路时保持其优势。

Abstract: Kerr-cat qubits have been experimentally shown to exhibit a large noise bias,
with one decay channel suppressed by several orders of magnitude. In
superconducting implementations, increasing the microwave drive on the
nonlinear oscillator that hosts the Kerr-cat qubit should, in principle,
further enhance this bias. Instead, experiments reveal that above a critical
drive amplitude the tunneling time - the less dominant decay channel - ceases
to increase and even decreases. Here, we show that this breakdown arises from
the multimode nature of the circuit implementation: specifically, the buffer
mode used to control the Kerr-cat qubit can induce multiphoton resonances that
sharply degrade Kerr-cat coherence if its frequency is not carefully chosen. We
uncover this mechanism by retaining the full circuit nonlinearities and
treating the strong drive exactly within a Floquet-Markov framework that
incorporates quasidegeneracies in the Kerr-cat spectrum. Our results not only
provide an explanation for the sudden reduction of the tunneling time but also
demonstrate the robustness of the Kerr-cat qubit when its surrounding
electromagnetic environment is carefully engineered.

</details>


### [51] [Quantum simulation of a noisy classical nonlinear dynamics](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.06198)
*Sergey Bravyi,Robert Manson-Sawko,Mykhaylo Zayats,Sergiy Zhuk*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: This paper presents a quantum algorithm for simulating noisy dynamics of classical nonlinear dissipative systems with many degrees of freedom. By adding Gaussian noise, they develop a method that scales efficiently on quantum computers, achieving significant computational advantage over classical methods. The algorithm's runtime dependency on system parameters is favorable, making it particularly relevant for large-scale simulations. The use of low-degree polynomial projections for solving the Kolmogorov equation is a key technical advance, and proving BQP-completeness highlights the algorithm's relevance for quantum computation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses the challenge of efficiently simulating complex classical systems using quantum computers. This is significant because quantum computers have the potential to offer exponential speedups in simulating quantum dynamics, but simulating classical systems presents unique challenges. The addition of weak Gaussian noise could lead to practical methods for noise-resilient simulations, which are crucial for many real-world applications. The proposed algorithm, achieving polynomial scaling in logarithmic system size, evolution time, and inverse error, suggests a promising direction for advancing quantum computational capabilities in this domain. Furthermore, the demonstration of BQP-completeness establishes that the simulation problem is as hard as quantum computation itself, setting a benchmark for understanding the computational complexity of such simulations.

Method: The method involves adding weak Gaussian noise to the classical system's equations of motion and initial state. This transforms the deterministic problem into a stochastic one, enabling the use of quantum algorithms for stochastic partial differential equations. A key component is projecting the Kolmogorov equation onto a space of low-degree polynomials, which allows efficient simulation by reducing the complexity of the system. This projection technique seems critical as it approximates the system dynamics with sufficient accuracy while keeping the computational load manageable. Additionally, the algorithm's BQP-completeness is proven by showing that solving the simulation problem is just as hard as simulating a universal quantum computer, indicating that the problem is inherently quantum and requires quantum resources for efficient computation.

Result: The result is a quantum algorithm that efficiently simulates noisy dynamics of nonlinear systems with large degrees of freedom. The scaling is favorable—polynomial in log N, evolution time, and inverse error. Importantly, it handles systems with specific sparsity and divergence-free conditions, which are common in nonlinear mechanics. The algorithm achieves this by leveraging low-degree polynomial approximations of the Kolmogorov equation and exploiting quantum computational power. Numerical simulations on an anharmonic oscillator and 2D Navier-Stokes equations demonstrate the algorithm's effectiveness, showing that classical simulations struggle but the quantum approach succeeds. This provides practical evidence for the algorithm's validity and performance, bridging the gap between theoretical results and real-world applications. The success of the quantum algorithm on these canonical nonlinear systems suggests broader applicability to other complex classical systems.

Conclusion: The paper conclusively demonstrates that quantum computers can efficiently simulate noisy dynamics of classical nonlinear dissipative systems with large degrees of freedom. By introducing Gaussian noise and using low-degree polynomial approximations, the algorithm achieves a quantum speedup with favorable scaling. The proof of BQP-completeness underscores the algorithm's fundamental computational complexity, showing it is as hard as any quantum computation. Numerical evidence from the simulations reinforces the method's practical value, particularly for systems where classical methods fall short due to computational limitations. This work opens up new possibilities for utilizing quantum computers to tackle complex classical simulations that are otherwise intractable, marking a significant step forward in quantum computational applications.

Abstract: We consider the problem of simulating dynamics of classical nonlinear
dissipative systems with $N\gg 1$ degrees of freedom. To make the problem
tractable for quantum computers, we add a weak Gaussian noise to the equation
of motion and the initial state. Our main result is an end-to-end quantum
algorithm for simulating the noisy dynamics of nonlinear systems satisfying
certain sparsity and divergence-free conditions. For any constant nonzero noise
rate, the quantum runtime scales polynomially with $\log{(N)}$, evolution time,
inverse error tolerance, and the relative strength of nonlinearity and
dissipation. Our main technical tool is the Kolmogorov partial differential
equation describing time evolution of scalar functions of solutions, averaged
over noise. To enable efficient quantum simulation, we project the Kolmogorov
equation onto the space of low degree polynomials and derive a rigorous upper
bound on the resulting approximation error, which may be of independent
interest. Finally, we show that the considered simulation problem is
BQP-complete, meaning that it is as hard as simulating the universal quantum
computer. We demonstrate the efficacy of our algorithm by simulating it
numerically for two paradigmatic nonlinear systems: an anharmonic oscillator
and the 2D Navier Stokes equation.

</details>

*Laura Cui,Thomas Schuster,Fernando Brandao,Hsin-Yuan Huang*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 该论文提出了一种高效生成近似单元傅里叶k-设计的方法，显著减少了量子电路的深度和所需辅币数量，并通过引入结构化随机单元格和新误差分析框架展现了其优势。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 该论文目的是在量子计算中如何高效地构建近似单元傅里叶k-设计，这对量子算法的分析和优化至关重要。

Method: 论文使用了结构化随机单元格，结合了长距离的二位量子门和低深度的随机经典哈希函数实现，这种方法显著减少了所需深度和辅币数量。

Result: 实验结果表明，该方法在所有参数（n, k, ε）上的深度呈现指数级优化，辅币和随机性消耗也得到了优化。

Abstract: We construct $\varepsilon$-approximate unitary $k$-designs on $n$ qubits in
circuit depth $O(\log k \log \log n k / \varepsilon)$. The depth is
exponentially improved over all known results in all three parameters $n$, $k$,
$\varepsilon$. We further show that each dependence is optimal up to
exponentially smaller factors. Our construction uses $\tilde{{O}}(nk)$ ancilla
qubits and ${O}(nk)$ bits of randomness, which are also optimal up to $\log(n
k)$ factors. An alternative construction achieves a smaller ancilla count
$\tilde{{O}}(n)$ with circuit depth ${O}(k \log \log nk/\varepsilon)$. To
achieve these efficient unitary designs, we introduce a highly-structured
random unitary ensemble that leverages long-range two-qubit gates and low-depth
implementations of random classical hash functions. We also develop a new
analytical framework for bounding errors in quantum experiments involving many
queries to random unitaries. As an illustration of this framework's
versatility, we provide a succinct alternative proof of the existence of
pseudorandom unitaries.

### [53] [Error Exponents for Quantum Packing Problems via An Operator Layer Cake Theorem](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.06232)
*Hao-Chung Cheng,Po-Chieh Liu*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: We prove a one-shot random coding bound for classical-quantum channel coding, recovering the reliability function for rates above the critical rate and extending to various quantum packing problems.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper proves a significant result in quantum communication, extending the reliability function to multi-shot scenarios and various quantum packing problems.

Method: Establishing an operator layer cake theorem to show the equivalence between pretty-good and randomized Holevo-Helstrom measurements.

Result: The one-shot random coding bound recovers the reliability function for classical-quantum channels above the critical rate and extends to various quantum communication problems.

Conclusion: The result is a significant step forward in classical communication over general quantum channels and quantum packing-type problems, with the operator layer cake theorem providing the technical foundation.

Abstract: In this work, we prove a one-shot random coding bound for classical-quantum
channel coding, a problem conjectured by Burnashev and Holevo in 1998. By
choosing the optimal input distribution, we recover the optimal error exponent
(i.e., the reliability function) of classical-quantum channels for rates above
the critical rate. Our result extends to various quantum packing-type problems,
including classical communication over any fully quantum channel with or
without entanglement-assistance, constant composition codes, and classical data
compression with quantum side information via fixed-length or variable-length
coding.
  Our technical ingredient is to establish an operator layer cake theorem - the
directional derivative of an operator logarithm admits an integral
representation of certain projections. This shows that a kind of pretty-good
measurement is equivalent to a randomized Holevo-Helstrom measurement, which
provides an operational explanation of why the pretty-good measurement is
pretty good.

</details>

Abstract: Twisted bilayer graphene (TBG) hosts a rich landscape of electronic phases

nontrivial band topology. While the flat bands near zero energy are central to

remains less understood. Here, we investigate these hybridization processes as
a function of the twist angle and analyze their impact on the charge
distribution, topological properties such as Chern number, quantum metric, and
orbital magnetic energy. We identify multiple topological phase transitions

momentum space. Notably, the central bands can exhibit phases with Chern
numbers C = 2, revealing previously unreported topological states in TBG.

A model is developed linking these factors, and conditions for avoiding morphological instabilities are derived based on wire dimensions and material properties.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper adds to understanding the mechanics of nanostructures under external stimuli, which is crucial for nanotechnology applications, especially in creating and controlling nanowires with desired properties.

Method: The authors created a model incorporating thermal effects, electromigration current, and adatom diffusion to study the dynamic behavior of the nanowire during necking.

Result: The model shows that with specific wire radii and lengths, a solid-state necking can be maintained before breaking, preventing morphological instabilities.

Conclusion: The findings provide guidelines for designing nanowires in materials science and nanotechnology, emphasizing the importance of wire dimensions in preventing failure during processing. Implications include optimizing manufacturing processes for reliable nanowire production.

Abstract: Axisymmetric solid-state necking of a single-crystal metallic nanowire in a
thermal contact with a substrate and subjected to a surface electromigration
current is accompanied by a local current crowding and a sharp rise of a
resistivity of a wire material in a thinning neck. This results in a
temperature spike at the neck, which feedback affects the necking via
thermomigration and the temperature-dependent surface diffusivity of the
adatoms. A model that incorporates these effects and couples the nonlinear
dynamics of a wire temperature and a wire radius for a necking wire is
presented. Conditions on the physical parameters are derived that ensure a
straight wire is in the solid state prior to an onset of a morphological
instability that ultimately breaks a wire via a pinch-off. The impacts of a
wire radius and a wire length on the temperature spike at the break junction
are studied.
